TORS: FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT AND PROCUREMENT
UNIT (DRAFT)
Background
Subsequent to the restoration of democracy and the revival of recovery efforts following more than
seven years of civil war and unrest, the Government of Sierra Leone (GOSL) is embarking on an
ambitious program of activities for national recovery and reintegration that will be supported by the
World Bank, the African Development Bank, the UK Department for International Development,
and other donor organizations. The National Programmes for: (i) Reconstruction, Rehabilitation and
Resettlement (RRR) and for (ii) Disarmament, Demobilisation and Reintegration (DDR) will
facilitate and finance reintegration support for ex-combatants and resettlement of refugees and
displaced people, rehabilitation of social and economic infrastructure, local institutional capacity
building and reconciliation assistance.
Two institutions will be the principal executing agencies under the World Bank, AfDB and other
donor supported projects: the National Commission for Rehabilitation, Reconstruction, and
Resettlement (NCRRR) and the National Committee on Disarmament, Demobilization, and
Reintegration (NCDDR). Both agencies are newly established and are temporary institutions that
will serve for a finite period of time to set the overall policy for the national programmes; ensure
adequate and appropriate coordination among and between relevant governmental, non-
governmental, and donor partners; and monitor implementation of specific sub-project activities.
Partner organizations including local and international non-governmental organizations, community
based organizations, UN agencies, line ministry departments, and private business will take principal
responsibility for the implementation of the project as sub-contractors.
The NCRRR will seek to facilitate national reconstruction activities through a demand driven social-
fund type financing mechanism (the Emergency Recovery Support Fund-- ERSF) that will support
community based sub-projects aimed at restoring economic and social infrastructure, promoting
reconciliation, and strengthening local institutions. Appropriate sub-projects will be identified by
war-affected populations and communities and designed and implemented in collaboration with
local and international NGOs, line ministries and other partners active and experienced in the
geographic and sectoral areas of concern. NCRRR, working through district-level officers, regional
offices, and inter-agency committees, will review and approve sub-project proposals, enter into
contract agreements with various implementing partners, and monitor the physical and financial
progress of sub-project implementation.
The NCDDR will oversee the GOSL commitment and efforts to completly disarm, demobilise and
reintegrate (i) an estimated 8,000 combatants of the Armed Forces of Sierra Leone (AFSL) and the
Revolutionary United Front (RUF) currently under Government control and (ii) an estimated 25,000
combatants of the Civil Defence Forces (CDF). The primary objectives are the consolidation of
security and the sustainable social and economic reintegration of ex-combatants. The disarmament,



Technical Annex                                   Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                   Attachment 5: Page 2 of 15
demobilisation and reintegration programme if implemented in a transparent and equitable manner,
could serve as an important pull factor for those combatants still holding out in the bush, provided a
conductive security environment is promoted. The Executive Secretariat of the NCDDR would be
responsible for ensuring: (i) the planning and implementation of the individual programme
components in collaboration with other government departments, NGOs and donors; (ii) the
transparent and accountable administration of the programme; and (iii) monitoring and evaluation.
An important financial and management control aspect of the DDR Programme will be the payment
of reintegration allowances to all ex-combatants noted above, and contracting and support for a
training and employment fund.
NCRRR and NCDDR are new institutions with limited experience administering donor-financed
project activities. In addition, the Government recognizes the need for the highest degree of
transparency and accountability in the operation and administration of the national programmes to:
(i) satisfy the requirements of donor agencies considering financial support to the GOSL efforts;
(ii) encourage implementing partners to continue collaborating with the Commission and the
Committee in the national recovery and reintegration process; and (iii) to reassure the public in
general as to the seriousness and commitment of the Government in redressing the damage and
causes of the civil war. Therefore, the GOSL intends to seek local and international technical
expertise to implement the financial management and procurement responsibilities for the
Emergency Recovery Support Fund and other donor-financed activities and support to the NCRRR
and NCDDR. Proposals will be sought from a short-list of qualified local and international firms.
The successful bidder will set-up and manage the Financial Management and Procurement Unit
(FMPU). This unit will have responsibility for all financial management functions, contracting, and
procurement procedures on behalf of the NCRRR and NCDDR. All costs associated with setting up
and operating the FMPU will be defined by the bidders and should be included in the Financial
Proposal. The bidders will have complete responsibility for identifying and hiring all local and
international staff deemed necessary to fulfil the responsibilities of the FMPU. The unit will be
managed by a qualified and experienced senior professional with experience in the design and
implementation of an appropriate financial management and internal control system for the Project
and Programme of this nature. Additional staff of accountants and other professionals will be
required as necessary to assist with disbursement, accounting, expenditure reviews, internal control
and project and sub-project procurement issues. An illustrative list of professional staff for the
FMPU is presented in these TORs, however the specific staffing arrangements for the unit are at the
discretion of the consultant firm bidding on these services.
The remaining pages outline in greater detail the terms of reference for the Financial Management
and Procurement Unit; required qualifications of manditory and recommended staff; and the timing,
duration, and duty post for the unit's staff.
1.    Overall Responsibilities
The Financial Management and Procurement Unit (FMPU) will support the National
Commission for Reconstruction, Resettlement and Rehabilitation (NCRRR) and the National
Committee on Disarmament, Demobilization and Reintegration (NCDDR) in all aspects of financial
management, accounting, contracting and procurement related to the GOSL's National Programmes.
The unit will be responsible for the following:



Technical Annex                                   Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                   Attachment 5: Page 3 of 15
1. Develop appropriate financial management and procurement policies and procedures (to
include standard formats, guidelines, etc.) in line with Government, and donors policies
and procedures; implement and enforce an adequate control system; and provide
training and support to NCRRR and NCDDR HQ and regional offices staff in their
implementation.
2. Design and set up a computerized financial management system (using off-the-shelf
software) that will provide for the adequate capture, analysis, and reporting of financial
information in an accurate and timely fashion for all funds and accounts allocated to
NCRRR and NCDDR for which FMPU will have full responsibility to manage. The
system should be design to handle various donors accounts (special accounts of the
World Bank and AfDB, Donors pool account, etc.) and to segregate all transactions and
reporting by category and by source.
3. Review all disbursements requests submitted by suppliers and implementing agencies for
goods and services provided to NCRRR and NCDDR and ensure propriety and
eligibility.
4. Effect payments to appropriate contractors and suppliers for goods and services
(including implementing partner sub-contracts) upon authorization by NCRRR and
NCDDR and verification of the availability of funds.
5. Ensure that all payment documentation is in order and in accordance with any special
requirements of various donor agencies.
6. Monitor contract payments and utilisation of advances to contractors.
7. Maintain up-to-date accounting records and ledgers, and record financial transactions for
all activities pertaining to NCRRR and NCDDR for which the FMPU is given
responsibility.
8. Maintain relevant local currency and foreign exchange bank accounts as authorized by
the Ministry of Finance, complete monthly reconciliation, and prepare monthly report of
expenses by category of expenditure for review and approval of NCRRR and NCDDR.
9. Ensure that special accounts are replenished according to donors policies and procedures.
10. Prepare appropriate statements of expenditure, direct payment and special payment
requests, and applications for replenishment of accounts per specific guidelines of donor
agencies for review, approval, and submission to the Ministry of Finance. Development
and Economic Planning (MOFDEP).
11. Prepare quarterly financial reports indicating expenses, commitments, and balances for
all expenditure categories by program component and individual sub-projects.
12. Facilitate any and all financial reviews of the funds and accounts under the authority of
Ministry of Finance, including, periodic audits and financial reviews by the GOSL's
Auditor General, or independent public accounting agencies as appointed by the Auditor
General.
13. Ensure that proper internal control system is in place to achieve accountability at all
levels



Technical Annex                                   Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                   Attachment 5: Page 4 of 15
14. Assist NCRRR. NCDDR and implementing partners as appropriate to procure goods and
services in compliance with all relevant procurement guidelines per agreement with
donor agencies and the appropriate procedures of the GOSL. In particular, help to
develop procurement documents for goods and services and ensure that the appropriate
approvals are sought from respective donor agencies as required.
15. Help to ensure adequate and appropriate expenditure analysis of sub-projects by the
regional offices and regional financial officers through staff training, periodic visits, and
monitoring the application of established procedures.
16. Conduct periodic spot checks of implementing agencies to ensure that adequate financial
management controls of NCRRR/NCDDR-financed activities are enforced.
17. Assist NCRRRlNCDDR in other areas related to their financial management, contracting
and procurement responsibilities under the NRRRP.
2.    Reporting Responsibilities
The Financial Management and Procurement Unit (FMPU) will be an autonomous body that
provides service for, and reports to, the National Commission for Reconstruction, Rehabilitation and
Resettlement, and to the National Committee on Disarnament, Demobilisation and Reintegration.
The FMPU will ensure that all contracting, procurement, disbursement and financial management
functions required under the two national programmes are carried out in accordance with standard
and accepted guidelines of the donor agencies supporting these two programmes. The Unit Manager
of the FMPU will report to the Commissioner of NCRRR and the Executive Secretary of NCDDR,
respectively, for the different monies provided to the GOSL for the respective programmes. The
FMPU will assist both NCRRR and NCDDR prepare all financial management reports, payment
requests, and other financial documentation required of the Commission and Committee by the
GOSL and donor agencies.
The FMPU will be responsible for the following reports:
1. Monthly Contract Expenditure Report (expenses by negotiated line item for reporting
period, year-to-date, and total-to-date; remaining balance by line item; and status of
advance payments);
2. Quarterly Contract Progress Report (work planned, carried out, accomplishments,
constraints, and planned activities for subsequent quarter);
3. Quarterly Donor Commitment Report (total expenses and commitments by donor and
cost category for reporting period, year-to-date, and total-to-date); and
4. Additional operational manuals, procedural guidelines, and ad hoc reports as reasonably
requested by the NCRRR and NCDDR.



Technical Annex                                    Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                    Attachment 5: Page 5 of 15
3.    Resources Management Responsibilities
It is estimated that the FMPU will have responsibility for overseeing the management of up to
US$50 million, however, currently proposed resources amount to around US$30 million. Of this
total, approximately $25 million will finance sub-projects implemented by partner organisations
active in the areas of resettlement, reconstruction, rehabilitation, training, etc. These activities will
be funded through sub-contract arrangements (ranging from $10,000 to $500,000 in value) for which
the FMPU will have financial monitoring responsibility. Implementing partners may be non-
governmental organisations, line ministry units, or community based organisations currently active
in Sierra Leone. The proposed financial mechanisms for the disbursement and control of funds
through these sub-contracts is discussed in detail in the attached document Operational Manualfor
the Emergency Recovery Support Fund (ERSF). The remaining $5 million will go toward
institutional support of the NCRRR and NCDDR; including the purchase of goods, equipment,
vehicles, technical assistance, and the payment of operating costs-- for which the FMPU will have
some responsibility for assisting with the procurement, disbursement and financial management.
In addition, it is expected that the FMPU will manage the mechanism for disbursing reintegration
payments to ex-combatants (to be done in either one or two payments, and either at central pre-
discharge centres, or in a limited number of regional centres or designated locations). It is currently
estimated that approximately 35,000 ex-combatants will receive some form of cash payment, a
control system for which will have to be developed by the FMPU. More specific details of the
proposed cash transfer arrangements for ex-combatants is provided in the attached document on the
Disarmament, Demobilization, and Reintegration Program.
The successful proposal must take into consideration the challenges posed by the current situation in
Sierra Leone and present a realistic approach to the issues raised by these programme elements and
respective responsibilities of the FMPU.
4.    Organizational structure
The FMPU will be managed by a firm with relevant international experience and track record in
similar donors funded projects involving similarly qualified personnel. The FMPU will be managed
by a senior Unit Manager, and be comprised of three units.
I -   Accounting and Disbursement Section: This section will be divided in two sub-
sections that will be responsible for the financial accounting and budgeting systems
(special account, disbursement) of NCRRR and NCDDR respectively. The two sub-
sections will co-ordinate and segregate the management of RRR and DDR funds.
Two line Accounting Managers (one for each institution) will be assigned to handle
the day-to-day financial transactions and accounting for each institution.
2 -   Procurement Section:  This section will ensure that all donors procurement
arrangements are strictly followed and enforced according to their requirements and
guidelines. In particular, the unit will be responsible for the preparation of necessary
bid documents, and will assist NCRRR and NCDDR with the procurement of



Technical Annex                                    Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                    Attachment 5: Page 6 of 15
approximately US$1 million of goods. The section may also provide some
assistance to partner organisations implementing sub-projects to prepare simplified
bid documents (for small-scale civil works) or to bulk procure some inputs such as
fertilizer.
3 -   Internal Control Section: This section will be managed by a Control Officer and will
be responsible for ensuring that all elements of the internal control system are carried
out efficiently. The unit will conduct, inter alia, random checking of payments
effected to various beneficiaries; verify that contracts and goods or services, etc.
have been executed and delivered by various contractors and suppliers as agreed; and
ensure that the internal procedures of both NCRRR and NCDDR are properly applied
by the staff of the institutions.
5.    Staffing
The FMPU will be headed by a qualified and experienced senior management professional with
experience in public administration, accounting, or project management with more than 10 years of
professional experience. The Manager of the Unit will oversee the work of the FMPU and report
directly to the Commissioner of NCRRR and the Executive Secretary of the NCDDR. It is expected
that the Manager will be supported by three to four professional staff who will be responsible for the
day-to-day accounting, procurement and internal control functions of the Unit.
Additional local staff will be required as necessary to assist with accounting, disbursement, control,
expenditure review and project and sub-project procurement issues. It is expected that the FMPU
will have an adequate complement of junior professional and support staff to fulfill its
responsibilities. The specific number and type of support staff to be present in the FMPU will be left
up to the discretion of the private institution awarded the contract for the set-up and operation of the
FMPU.
The consultant firm will be responsible for the recruitement, hiring and compensation of all staff of
the FMPU.
6.    Special and Project Accounts
The GOSL (through the Ministry of Finance) will authorize the FMPU to open and operate
necessary special and project accounts on behalf of NCRRR and NCDDR for donors and GOSL
counterpart funding programmes. The FMPU will manage these accounts and make payments to
vendors, contractors and individual beneficiaries (in the case of ex-combatants) once authorized to
do so by NCRRR and NCDDR. All accounts managed by FMPU will be operated with two
signatures, of which one must always be the FMPU Manager. For funds that support NCRRR
activities, either the Commissioner or Deputy Commissioner, NCRRR, will counter-sign checks; for
funds that support NCDDR activities, either the Executive Secretary or his representative will
counter-sign. Special payment requests and withdrawal applications for replenishment to donors
must also be signed by the authorized representative of the Ministry of Finance upon request by
either the Executive Secretary of NCDDR or the Commissioner of NCRRR.



Technical Annex                                    Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                    Attachment 5: Page 7 of 15
7.    Audit
By law in Sierra Leone, the GOSL Auditor General is responsible for auditing public funds.
However, considering the heavy volume of work already assigned to the Auditor General's
Department, the exceptional situation, and logistic adjustment the Government ministries and
agencies are going through, and that the continuing viability of the ERSF and DDR programmes
demands prompt periodic auditing of their accounts, it is recommend that the Auditor General
delegate the auditing of the ERSF and DDR funds to an external auditing firm appointed by him for
that purpose. Semi-annual audits will be required of all accounts under the control of the FMPU.
8.    Timing, Duration and Work Station
The contract for the FMPU Consultant firn will be for three (3) years, subject to performance. It is
expected that the contract for these technical assistance services would be signed between the GOSL
and the successful bidder towards the end of CY 1998. Therefore, all responsive bids must indicate
that all proposed staff would be able to take up post by this time.
All staff of the FPMU will be based in Freetown, Sierra Leone, however, some travel will be
required to the provincial cities and district headquarters in order to assist in monitoring the regional
financial officers and implementing partners. It is expected that FMPU staff will be required to
travel up-country approximately 5 days per quarter.
9.    Services, Equipment and Materials Provided by GOSL
The Government will provide to the Consultant all necessary licenses, pernits, duty-free waivers for
office equipment and for personal goods of expatriate staff, and relevant reports, etc., necessary for the
set up and operation of the FMPU. However, all required goods, equipment, furnishings and other
essential inputs needed for the Financial Management and Procurement Unit should be included as part
of the Consultants Financial Proposal.

FMPU Staff Terms of Reference:
FMPU Manager
The Government of Sierra Leone (GOSL) is in the process of finalising agreements with the World
Bank, AfDB and other donors to support the National Resettlement, Reconstruction, and
Rehabilitation and the Disarmaement, Demobilisation and Reintegration Programmes. Two
institutions will be the principal executing agencies under the World Bank, AfDB and other Donors
supported programmes: the National Commission for Rehabilitation, Reconstruction, and
Resettlement (NCRRR) and the National Committee on Disarmament, Demobilization, and
Reintegration (NCDDR). The GOSL is calling for the establishment of a unit, the Financial
Management and Procurement Unit (FMPU), which will have full responsibility for all financial
management, control and procurement tasks under the donor-assisted portions of the two national
programmes. This unit will be contracted out to a qualified private firm and will be headed up by an
experienced professional manager whose responsibilities and qualifications are noted below.
Duties and Responsibilities:
Responsible to the Commissioner for National Commission for Reconstruction, Resettlement and
Rehabilitation (NCRRR), and the Executive Secretary for National Committee for Disarmament,
Demobilization and Reintegration (NCDDR) for operational issues, the FMPU Manager will provide
general administrative and financial management support to NCRRR and NCDDR. The FMPU
Manager will oversee all accounting, fund administration, procurement and internal control
responsibilities under World Bank, AfDB and other Donors programmes.  Specifically the
incumbent's main responsibilities will be to:
* Liaise with the Ministry of Finance and all donors in overseeing and managing the special and
project accounts established for the implementation of activities under the National Programmes
for Reconstruction, Resettlement and Rehabiliation, and for Disarmament, Demobilization and
Reintegration;
* Ensure that all financial mechanisms are set up (financial books, ledgers, files, etc.) for the
appropriate management and control of financial resources made available to the Commissioner
of NCRRR and the Executive Secretary of NCDDR;
* Approve payment requests after ensuring their propriety and eligibility, and verifying the
availability of funds;
* Review and sign checks and other payment mechanisms for counter signature by designated
personal: the Commissioner of NCRRR or his Deputy, the Executive Secretary of NCDDR or his
Representative, or The Ministry of Finance or its Representative;
* Ensure the maintenance of up-to-date project and financial accounts;



Technical Annex                                    Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                   Attachment 5: Page II of 15
* Supervise internal control activities;
* Supervise procurement activities;
* Ensure the Unit assets are accounted for (vehicles, computers, etc.);
* Prepare NCRRR/NCDDR and FMPU staff salaries;
* Supervise and conduct in-house training and relevant training program of staff for the unit;
* Arrange and facilitate any audit or financial review as called for by the Donors agencies, World
Bank, AfDB or the Government of Sierra Leone's Auditor General;
* Provide necessary support for the regional finance officers in carrying out their responsibilities;
*  Undertake other official duties assigned by the Commissioner of NCRRR and the Executive
Secretary of NCDDR.
Minimum Qualifications and Experience Required
- Master in Economics, Accounting major, or similar.
- Ten years of post-qualification experience as accountant supervisor, project accountant and/or
project manager
* Familiarity with World Bank, AfDB and donors financial management, contracting, and
procurement procedures.
Proven competence in the use of computer software applications including accounting software,
spreadsheets, database and word-processing packages highly desirable.
Conditions of Service
The incumbent will be employed directly by the Consultant firm, eligible for all standard benefits
usually provided by (and indicated in a personnel policy manual of) the successful firm, and
available to take up responsibilities on or around 1st January 1999. The services described above
will be performed predominantly in Freetown, however, some travel to the provincial cities and
villages will be required as security allows.



Technical Annex                                    Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                    Attachment 5: Page 12 of i5
FMPU Staff Terms of Reference:
Accounting Manager
Duties and Responsibilities
Reporting directly to the FMPU Manager the incumbent will:
1. Assist the FMPU Manager to co-ordinate various activities with the Commissioner of NCRRR
and the Executive Secretary of NCDDR, Regional Offices and implementing agencies,
consultants, suppliers, contractors, etc.
2. Liaise with commercial banks on matters concerning the special and project accounts on
financial activities of NCRRR or NCDDR;
3. Prepare checks and other payment mechanisms for signature by FMPU Manager, the

DDR Program: Reintegration Component;
Considerations and Technical Assistance Needs
1.    Background
The GOSL has demonstrated solid commitment to the DDR as evidenced by a credible process, shaped
by clear and consistent policy pronouncement, supported with a functioning policy committee unit and an
Executive Secretariat - both constituting the institutional framework for managing and coordinating the
DDR program.
However limited financial resources and sporadic incursions by the rebel forces represent major
challenges to the initiation of a comprehensive disarmament, demobilization and reintegration program.
Compounding the process is the urgency of time, which holds out the inevitable option of a planning and
implementation depth atypical of conventional DDR programs. Designed to take place in a very difficult
socio-economic environment, the process offers limited possibilities for creating stable livelihoods in the
short term. Consequently, the envisaged reintegration of 2,200 members of the ex-AFSL and the
captured/surrendered members of the RUF currently encamped in Lungi garrison, is fraught with a
considerable number of complexities.
The process of initial military screening, registration, socio-economic profiling of the target groups, pre-
discharge orientation activities (socio-psychological counseling, civic education as well as vocational and
skills orientation) and discharge are planned to take place between August 1998 and January 1999 - a
five month timeframe considered insufficient by any standard. Although the cumulative and extended
period of encampment has engendered an intense and restless feeling of uneasiness among the
combatants, it has also fostered an expectation of quick discharge and reintegration into civilian life - an
expectation that cannot be overlooked in the planning and implementation of the reintegration process.
The reintegration component of the DDR program is envisioned to be an integral part of an overall
national reconciliation and reconstruction strategy. It is proposed that demobilization will take place in
three phases, between July 1998 and January 2000. Phase I, referring to the currently detained
AFSL/RUF ex-combatants in Lungi (LDC), was scheduled for July 1998 to January 1999. However, to
facilitate the reintegration of these ex-combatants into civilian life a concerted effort needs to be put in
place, involving all stakeholders, to develop a careful and realistic strategy which can be implemented in
the very near future.
In this respect the Government of Sierra Leone faces considerable challenges. These challenges need to
be met to avoid the many risks associated with re-entry of ex-combatants into a civilian society
devastated and traumatized by a protracted and destructive civil war.
The planning process of the DDR reintegration component will address two immediate issues. Firstly, a
series of activities need to be in place at LDC to ensure that the already started demobilization and
reintegration process of ex-AFSL in the camp can proceed in an appropriate and meaningful manner. It
should be recalled that prior to the launching of the improved camp management and the provision of
food and other basic needs by DFID considerable tension had been building up in and around LDC.
Recent improvement of living conditions and the ongoing registration and profiling exercise have
improved the morale in LCD. A failure to follow through with concrete social and economic reintegration



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                      Attachment 7: Page 2 of 14
initiatives during the encampment period may have a great impact on the success or failure of the entire
demobilization process. The social and political viability of the remainder of the DDRP could therefore
be at risk.
Secondly, a detailed and credible plan for the reinsertion and reintegration of the subsequent phases of the
DDRP needs to be developed. This plan needs to take into account the significant different starting points
for social and economic reintegration for the ex-AFSL, ex-RUF and ex-CDF combatants, respectively.
The design and planning of the social and economic reintegration measures needs to be consistent with
the following overall principles:
*   Targeted assistance to ex-combatants will only be provided during the reinsertion phase;
*  From the outset, longer-term reintegration assistance to ex-combatants will make optimal
use of the mechanisms established under the RRR;
*  Assistance to vulnerable groups such as female ex-combatants, disabled ex-combatants and
child ex-combatants needs to utilize and strengthen the existing in-country capacity of
organizations already on the ground.
2.    Strategy Framework for Social and Economic Reintegration
To prepare the ex-combatants adequately for their re-entry into civilian life, the DDR reintegration
framework needs to incorporate the following components:
* Social reintegration, including both socio-psychological counseling and civic education;
* These components are intended to address psychological factors, which distort patterns of
behavior while providing the ex-combatants with positive attitudes towards civic
responsibilities, respect for democratic culture and skills for conflict resolution.
Economic reintegration, including vocational and post-discharge orientation. The focus of economic
reintegration is to equip the ex-combatants with productive skills and options for employment as effective
means to successful transition to civilian life.  The proposed Training and Employment Fund,
employment-intensive public works and promotion of artisan enterprise development are variety of
programs designed to serve this purpose and provide linkage with the emergency recovery social fund.
Community sensitization and information campaign:
* A major precondition for successful reintegration of ex-combatants is the receptiveness of
their various communities regarding their return and resettlement. Pervasive feelings of
mistrust, animosity and other forms of social tension engendered by war calls for a
systematic process of re-engineering social relationships and perceptions. Conversely, to
accommodate reintegration of ex-combatants, specific attitudinal transformation needs to be
inculcated in the returning ex-combatants to prepare them for eventual reintegration in the
local communities. These processes require the design of a comprehensive program of
community sensitization and information dissemination.
Within the context of the DDR program, an Information and Community Sensitization is anticipated to
focus on (i) the ex-combatants currently encamped in Lungi; (ii) the intended communities of return;
(iii) as well as a nationwide audience. Detailed planning for each component needs to be developed
within a couple of weeks with overlapping and incremental implementation process. The constraints of



Technical Annex                                       Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                        Attachment 7: Page 3 of 14
time not only demand concurrent planning but also simultaneous implementation of the strategy
components.
3.    Analysis of expectation and target group profiles
During the registration of the ex-combatants a short socio-economic profile will be established. These
socio-economic profiles form the baseline infornation on educational background, professional
experience and future professional expectations of the ex-combatants. The analysis of these profiles
should provide useful information to the reintegration planners and implementers in terms of areas of
district of re-settlement, the requirements to facilitate return to the respective districts, intended
occupations and relevant skills requirements. The socio-economic data collected from the registration
process and from the rapid inventory of skills among the ex-combatants are essential to program both
social and economic reintegration initiatives. Convergence of skills with chosen district of settlement and
opportunities for employment in the local labor market are crucial in achieving anticipated results of any
vocational improvement and employment generation program.
4.    Training needs assessment and identification of skills gaps
To support the social and economic reintegration process it is further recommended to carry out a rapid
training needs assessment in the formal and informal sectors of the Sierra Leone economy. This training
needs assessment could be carried out through an establishment survey and/or through the use of rapid
urban and rural appraisal techniques. Parallel to this training needs assessment a rapid appraisal of
economic opportunities could be carried out. More insight into the skill requirements of the labor market
and potential market niches will enable the ex-combatants to make a more informed choice regarding
their employment and income generating opportunities. This type of assessment would also inform
training providers about the current level and quantity of skills demand, identify the skill gaps and
facilitate the design of means to fill these gaps.
5.    Local implementation capacity and requirement for upgrading
A rapid assessment of local capacity will provide a valid basis for a rational choice of implementing
partners in the reintegration program. The capacity of existing local institutions to deliver the required
program for skills improvement and to participate in the reconstruction and rehabilitation program
remains unclear. Considerable looting and destruction of the facilities of most local institutions remains a
major constrain. This becomes obvious when contrasted against the sizeable capital investment required
to upgrade their equipment. Under the current time constraints, the mission recommends to initiate
immediate pilot activities to test the potential for upgrading capacity of local institutions to provide on-
site training orientation and other components of the reintegration program for the phase 1 operation in
Lungi. However, balancing the requirement for upgrading of local institutional capacity against the
exigency of engaging foreign expertise remains a delicate decision that will influence the quality, time
and cost of program delivery. Technical Assistance will be required to assist in the design of program and
management of the process.



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                      Attachment 7: Page 4 of 14
6.    Options for reintegration
During the encampment the possibilities for organizing an extensive skills training program will be
limited due to the time constraints under which the reintegration program is being developed. However,
the data and information to be derived from the socio-economic profiles, the economic opportunities and
training needs assessment, and the assessment of local implementation capacities are essential building
blocks for developing an appropriate vocational orientation program for the ex-combatants. The
vocational orientation would have to be planned and implemented with the assistance of local training
providers who have developed or are in the process of developing tailor-made short courses for ex-
combatants. Within the framework of this orientation, the possibility of organizing on-site workshops and
on-site trade exhibitions would have to be explored with those training providers. Such workshops or
such an exhibition of the use and content of a variety of skills would facilitate a more informed career
choice for the ex-combatants. A more comprehensive training program will be developed and provided
within the context of the Training and Employment Fund.
After the discharge, a rmenu of different social and economic reintegration options could be available to
the ex-combatants. Recent plans for reintegration assistance in other post-conflict situations have
included all, a combination of or some of the following:
- Rehabilitation of basic social, economic and physical infrastructure;
Revitalization of basic social services;
* Community-based rural development programs;
L Labor-intensive public works programs;
- Agricultural programs
- Skill development in technical and/or entrepreneurial skills to facilitate employment or self-
employment (including apprenticeships);
- Adult education (literacy, numeracy, life-skills, etc.);
* Self-employment through the creation of small and micro enterprises;
*  Provision of micro-credit, self-employment tool kits, and support services (counseling and
guidance, job placement, etc.) for assisting reintegration into different activities;
*  Targeted activities for vulnerable groups, such as, disabled ex-combatants, child soldiers,
etc.;
Within the context of the DDR reintegration component, it is important to recommend realistic options to
the ex-combatants. DDR will therefore be responsible for the provision of counseling and referral
services at the regional and district level, which will provide ex-combatants with information about
potential opportunities for employment, participation in the private sector, and community-based
reconstruction and rehabilitation activities. It is important to note that in principle the implementation
strategy of the CRRP is to use a community-based demand driven project identification and development
process. Ex-combatants will additionally have access to an employment, vocational training and
apprenticeship fund known as the regional Training and Employment Fund (TEF). The TEF will facilitate
access to apprenticeships or other skills training, and will subsidize employment opportunities where
possible.
As far as post-discharge social reintegration is concerned, a community sensitization and information
campaign for ex-combatants, communities and the general public will be essential. This has already been
emphasized by GOSL as an issue of overarching importance. Important steps have been taken so far,
including public announcement of the terms and conditions of the DDRP as well as a high profile
televised debate and information program on the DDRP. These initiatives need to be followed up by a



Technical Annex                                       Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                        Attachment 7: Page 5 of 14
more detailed and well-planned sensitization campaign. Such a campaign would have the following
elements: (i) immediate community level sensitization in and around LDC based on, and in collaboration
with, the considerable potential of local groups, networks and individuals that each in their own way are
working towards practical community based reconciliation; (ii) a national level campaign, through the
print media, radio and television and other appropriate means; (iii) sensitization in the region prior to and
in concurrence with the establishment of the DDRP's Regional Reintegration Offices; (iv) community
level campaigns in preparation for the return of ex-combatants. It is furthennore essential that this
sensitization campaign links up concretely with the different youth development activities and the
participatory consultation exercises that are currently being undertaken by various local and international
organizations.
7.    Design consideration and implementation requirements.
Major design considerations are as follows:
*   Relevance and quality of the content of training program and other forms of reintegration
assistance to the ex-combatants to constitute sufficient inducement and motivation to
participate in on-camp and off-camp programs.
*   Capacity for rapid and on-site deployment by delivering agencies contracted to implement
specific component of the reintegration program is vital for flexibility in the design and
implementation of the program
*   Options for incremental reintegration through public works-labor-intensive programs and
phased assistance to support initial re-insertiation allowance are critical to reducing not only
a dominant impression of rewarding rebellion but also fostering community acceptance of
the ex-combatants.
*   Orientation towards acquisition of life-skills and enterprise development support should
drive the process of vocational training and other reintegration assistance. Within this
context, the option of private sector participation should be explored.
8.    Technical Assistance Requirements
Within the context of the DDR reintegration program technical assistance will be required to assist the
Secretariat in the planning and design of the reintegration activities for the ex-combatants currently
encamped in Lungi. It is recommended to provide the Secretariat with a social reintegration specialist, an
economic reintegration specialist and a community sensitization specialist. The terms of reference for
these positions are attached.

Sierra Leone                                                     Attachment 7: Page 6 of 14
Draft Terms of Reference
Reinsertion and Reintegration Unit Manager
National Committee for Disarmament, Demobilization and Reintegration (NCDDR)
Executive Secretariat
Background
In June 1998, following more than seven years of civil war and illegal junta rule, the recently
reinstated Government of Sierra Leone (GOSL) took the initiative to develop a comprehensive
disarmament, demobilization and reintegration (DDR) program aimed at dealing with an estimated
35,000 ex-combatants including members of the Revolutionary United Front (RUF), Armed Forces of
sierra Leone, and the Civil Defense Forces. Considerable progress was made to initiate work under this
DDR program during the last six months, however, an upsurge in fighting in late 1998, culminating in an
attack on and battle for Freetown in early January 1999, resulted in the suspension of the program.
ECOMOG forces were able to re-establish security in Freetown and Western region and cleared major
highways to allow access to the country.
Subsequent to the attack on Freetown, there is a growing understanding that for sustainable long-
term peace and security in the country, a political settlement is preferable. Consequently the UN, in
concert with major bilateral partners, facilitated a peace negotiation between rebel leader Sankoh and
RUF commanders as well as the Government and other Rebel groups. The outcome was the Lome Peace
Agreement which provided the basis for a negotiated settlement to the conflict. Under the specific
provision of the agreement, the United Nation Military Observer Mission (UNOMSIL) and Monitoring
Group of West African States (ECOMOG) will enforce cease fire and oversee the disarmament,
demobilization of all surrendered forces as part of the comprehensive DDR program.
In anticipation of a rapid resolution of the current conflict, international partners of the GOSL
made committments to assist the Government re-start and plan for the expansion of its' DDR Program.
The Program is seen as crucial in moving forward the recently negotiated peace agreement, sustain a
viable cease-fire agreement as well as provide vital momentum to sustainable peace and longer-term
security. Specifically, long-term technical assistance position would be required to manage the various
aspects of the Reintegration measures which have been identified to support successful return of
demobilised ex-combatants under the DDR program of the Executive Secretariat of the NCDDR. Given
the special nature of the DDR responsibilities, and the lack of in-country experience in these areas, as
well as to maintain credibility and neutrality in the program, it is recommended that selected candidate
will serve as unit technical manager in the related area and maintain overall responsibility for the day to
day management of the program of their respective units within Executive Secretariat of NCDDR to
which they will be attached. The responsibilities outline below represent the broad terms of reference for
the Reinsertion and Reintegration Unit Manager.
Context
The purpose of the DDR Program is to facilitate the process whereby combatants from both sides
of the conflict gradually and peacefully return to normal and productive civilian lives. Specifically, the
DDR would finance activities aimed at disarming and demobilizing combatants (including registration,
medical screening, and socio-economic profiling, pre-discharge orientation programs), providing
reinsertion assistance (including departure allowances, transitional safety net allowance and facilitating
access to land) and reintegration support (including vocational and/or non-formal education,
apprenticeships, information and referral services, counseling, community relations and civic education).



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                      Attachment 7: Page 7 of 14
An effective Reinsertion and Reintegration program would provide for ex-combatants opportunities to
become productive members of their home communities. The opportunities would involve activities in
support of social and economic reintegration assistance beginning with the pre-discharge orientation
activities during demobilization, transitional allowances upon discharge and training, employment and
self employment upon settlement in home communities. The candidate should respond with great degree
of flexibility and creativity to the fast changing conditions on the ground.
Objective
To oversee the design and implementation of the Reinsertion and Reintegration program for
approximately 45,000 ex-combatants, that is aimed to facilitate their return to civilian life and consolidate
the peace and security and form the basis for post-war community reintegration and rehabilitation in
close consultation and co-ordination with NCRRR.
Responsibilities:
The Reinsertion and Reintegration unit Manager will report directly to the Executive Secretary , in
consultation with the chief technical advisor and other unit managers, maintain close working relationship
and co-operations with UN Agencies (ILO, WFP, UNDP, and UNICEF) NGOs, firms, and traditional
leadership. The R&R Unit Manager will be responsible for the definition, implementation, management,
and evaluation as well as revision of strategies aimed at facilitating the social, psychological and
economic reintegration of all eligible ex-combatants under the Government's DDR Program. The Unit
manager will manage day to day operation of the reinsertion and reintegration program as well as design
specific measure for promoting incremental assumption of line responsbility by a suitably identified local
counterpart.
Specifically, the incumbent will be responsible to:
1. In close consultation with chief technical advisor, technical consultants and other unit managers,
review strategies and proposed implementation mechanisms for the Government's reintegration
program and recommend adjustments and/or improvements;
2. Identify and assess capacities of organizations (NGOs, public and private sector institutions) to
implement program activities including: socio-psychological counseling, civic education, community
sensitization, vocational training, public works, micro-grant schemes, non-formal education, and
targeted assistance to disabled and child combatants, etc.;
3. Analyze the expectations, preferences and needs of ex-combatants to facilitate their successful
reintegration into Sierra Leonean society; based on these analyses, develop terms of reference and
assist with the preparation of relevant bidding documents to be used in contracting participating
organizations to implement reintegration activities;
4. Conduct the technical review of proposals in consultation with other unit managers, chief technical
advisor and approve of reintegration program activities to be financed under the DDR Program and
its Training and Employment Program (TEP) fund; refine procedures of the TEP based on the
changing circumstances.
5. In collaboration with NCRRR's Information and Sensitization Unit, identify appropriate messages
and delivery mechanisms for civic education and community sensitization activities and facilitate
dissemination through appropriate media channels and the Regional Reintegration Offices (RROs);
6. Jointly with the chief technical advisor and relevant unit managers, oversee the implementation of



Technical Annex                                       Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                        Attachment 7: Page 8 of 14
the provision of transitional safety net allowances.
7. Work with M&E unit to design in-depth tracer studies, and analyze appropriate performance data on
reintegration efforts to allow for proper program planning and monitoring;
8.  Supervise and ensure that all sub-contractors providing NCDDR with services related to pre-
discharge orientation, social and economic reintegration, and community sensitization are performing
in accordance with their contracts and generally accepted professional standards;
9. Assess performance and impact of on-going reintegration efforts, prepare quarterly reports for the
Executive Secretary as to performance, and recommend adjustments to program strategies as required
and in line with intelligence data and report from the M&E unit;
10. Design and supervise technical studies and survey to adapt program strategies and evaluate the level
of reintegration on the part of the ex-combatants targeted in the program.
11. Draft R&R unit's administrative systems and establish regional reintegration offices, recruit qualified
technical national and regional staff, and prepare work plans as well as operations budget on Bi-
annual basis
12. Assist the ES to identify and build relevant in-country capacity by conducting necessarytrainings for
the up-grading of local unit staff.
13. On period basis invite appropriate counterparts of the technical co-ordination committee to discuss
issues, update and refine design, implementation and monitoring of R&Ractivities.Identify relevant
international contacts with individuals, institutions and projects that could be called upon to help
strengthen the GOSL/DDR Program and staff;
14. Collaborate with all other relevant technical and administrative units within and outside of NCDDR
to facilitate the successful implementation of Government's DDR strategies.
Minimum Qualifications
At a minimum, the incumbent would possess the following capabilities and qualifications:
*  post-graduate degree in social sciences, economics, non-formal education/vocational training,
social work, business administration, international development or other relevant fields
*  10 or more years of professional experience of which at least 5 years has been spent working
directly for similar reintegration efforts for ex-combatants,
*  detailed knowledge of and training in at least one of the three areas of reintegration (social,
psychological or economic) and additional experience with at least one other area,
*  at least 5 years of managerial experience that involved the development and implementation of
specific work plans, overseeing technical staff, and supervising the work of sub-contractors,
*  long-term resident experience working in a developing country implementing a similar programs,
significant experience working in Africa; work experience in West Africa and Sierra Leone
desirable,
* demonstrated ability to work effectively in a team of international and local staff in a dynamic,
highly politicized, and sometimes logistically constrained, environment,
* knowledge of and experience working with Government institutions and with NGOs,

Community Sensitization Specialist
NCDDR / NCRRR
Draft Terms of Reference
Background:
A major precondition for successful reintegration of ex-combatants is the receptiveness of their various
communities regarding their return and resettlement. Pervasive feelings of mistrust, animosity and other
forms of social tension engendered by war demand the establishment of a systematic process of re-
establishing social relationships and perceptions. Conversely, to accommodate the reintegration of ex-
combatants, specific attitudinal transformation needs to be inculcated in the returning ex-combatants to
prepare them for eventual reintegration in the local communities. These processes require the design of a
comprehensive program of community sensitization and information dissemination.
Within the context of the DDR program, an Information and Community Sensitization specialist will be
required to assist the Executive Secretariat of the NCDDR and the NCRRR in the planning and design of
an information and sensitization campaign. The campaign will target (i) the ex-combatants currently
encamped in Lungi (ii) the intended communities of return (iii) as well as nationwide audience.
Initially, the task will cover a period of six weeks, starting from the second week of September 1998. If
necessary, a follow-up mission might be necessary to evaluate the impact and fine-tune the sensitization
and reintegration program. The assignment will outline activities for raising social awareness and civic
responsibilities and will essentially include the following: (i) an assessment of existing local capacities
and the framework for coordination of the process; (ii) the design of a comprehensive national strategy
on reconciliation and social rehabilitation; (iii) the development of broad content and message and (iv)
the identification of credible mechanism for the delivery of message.
Duties and Responsibilities:
The specific responsibilities of the specialist will comprise the following:
*   Analyze the capacity and identify potential implementing agencies in the field of
information and community sensitization.
*   Direct the preparation of comprehensive national strategy for community sensitization.
*   Assist implementation agencies in designing target specific programs of re-engineering
social conception regarding the ex-combatants and other war-affected groups.
*   Workout strategies for collaboration with national and international agencies currently
operating in the field of community sensitization.
*   Assess and review the effectiveness of the message and content of the community
sensitization program as well as ascertain the effectiveness of the medium of information
dissemination.
*   Develop terms of reference, procedures, criteria and performance indicators as the basis for
contracting implementing agencies and monitoring results.
*   Assist in the review and identification appropriate programs of community sensitization.
*   Elaborate implementation plans, phasing and the budgets for the Executive Secretariat.



Technical Annex                                       Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                       Attachment 7: Page 11 of 14
*   Support the Secretariat in the coordination and the management of the process of
sensitization campaign in collaboration with a lead local agency.
*   Co-operate with the reintegration specialists to develop linkages with community-based
initiatives and reintegration schemes, which are designed to promote effective resettlement
of ex-combatants in their respective communities.
*  Elaborate and introduce relevant management instruments to monitor the impact of the
program.



Technical Annex                                             Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                              Attachment 7: Page 12 of 14
Terms of Reference - M&E Unit manager
The monitoring and evaluation Unit Manager oversees the implementation of the unit's activities so that
timely, accurate and effective information is available for programme management and planning
purposes. It is envisioned that based in the required qualifications and experience this position will be
recruited internationally.
The core of the monitoring and evaluation unit for the NCDDR will incorporate a Unit Manager, acting
as team leader and directly responsible for interfacing with the other unit managers and the Executive
Secretary. The Unit Manager will be supported by a Data Analyst / Statistician, in charge of reporting
programme outcomes and manage all analytical procedures, a Systems Administrator who will supervise
the data entry team and will maintain the necessary systems and equipment, and a Senior Programme
Monitor in charge of the day to day follow-up of programme activities.
In order to facilitate the monitoring of on-going activities, particularly those implemented by institutional
partners, and to facilitate capturing qualitative information aboutprogramme impact, the unit will rely on
a decentralised team of Field Programme Monitors. These will liaise with the Regional Reintegration
Offices to follow-up on programme activities, maintain a running sample of beneficiaries' perceptions
and visit active implementing partners. The Field Programme Monitors be coordinated and will report to
the Senior Programme Monitor located in the central office.
The following picture depicts the proposed organisational chart for the ES-NCDDR's M&E Unit.
All positions are proposed based in the functions and responsibilities described, without
consideration for the two positions already existing in the Unit or their respective position names.
This does not mean that existing staff must not be considered for the new proposed structure, but
rather than the positions and responsibilities need to be re-examine to respond the proposed new
functions.

Responsibilities
He/she will be responsible for the maintenance, updating and reporting on monitoring and evaluation data
related to all aspects of support provided by NCDDR to eligible ex-combatants under the GoSL's DDR
Programme. Specifically, the incumbent responsibilities will include:
1. In collaboration with unit managers and programme advisor/CTA, review and maintain as necessary
registration requirements and existing procedures for data collection and processing in regards to
military screening, identification and socio-economic profiling of ex-combatants;
2. Monitor and ensure the integrity of the data collected by all units in the disarmament, demobilisation
and reintegration process for all ex-combatants;
3. Develop and carry out appropriate training activities for Unit staff and implementing partner
personnel for general and specific M&E techniques, M&E system procedures and reporting
requirements;
4. Ensure proper reporting of performance indicators on the part of implementing partners and NCDDR
units carrying out DDR Programme activities;
5. Oversight the development of systems and specific mechanisms to allow for the sharing of
programme and sub-project performance data with financial data being collected by the Financial
Management and Procurement Unit;
6. Design and oversee the implementation of specialized studies aimed at assessing the impact of
specific areas of assistance under the DDR Programme;
7. In collaboration with key partners such as the National Commission for Reconstruction,
Rehabilitation and Resettlement (NCRRR) and UNICEF, review data sharing needs to help ensure
basic compatibility with other institutional databases and M&E systems;
8. On periodic basis invite appropriate counterparts of the technical co-ordination committee to discuss
issues, update and refine procedures, reporting formats, data collection and forms.
9. Co-ordinate the preparation of specialized reports based on existing data as requested by the ES,
programme advisors/CTA, unit managers and members of NCDDR, or donor agencies supporting the
Government's DDR Programme, and facilitate supervision and evaluation missions of the later.
Qualifications
* Graduate degree in social sciences, international development, public administration, or other
relevant field,
*  10 years of professional experience of which at least 5 years have been spent working directly in
programme monitoring and evaluation for DDR activities, post-conflict or social development
projects,
*  Formal training or experiential knowledge in management information systems,
*  Long-term resident experience working in a developing country implementing similar programmes,
significant experience working in Africa; work experience in West Africa and Sierra Leone desirable,
a Demonstrated ability to work effectively in a team of international and local staff in a dynamic,
highly politicised, and sometimes logistically constrained, environment,
* Knowledge of and experience working with Government institutions, International community and
with NGOs,
*  Excellent spoken and written English,

TORs: Project Financial Audit
Objective
The objective of the audit of the Program Financial Statement (PFS) is to enable the auditor to express a
professional opinion on the financial position of the various donors funds (World Bank, AfDB, other
Donors) allocated to the National Resettlement, Reconstruction, and Rehabilitation Program and managed
by the Financial Management and Procurement Unit (FMPU) at each fiscal year, semi-annually for three
(3) years, starting from June 30, 1999. The auditor is also required to express separate opinions on the
Statement of Expenditures (SOEs) and the Special Accounts (SA) for the funds received and
expenditures occurred for the accounting period ended at the same dates. It is also expected to express
separate opinions on the accounts for other donors according to their reporting requirements.
The program accounts (books of account) provide the basis for preparation of the PFS and are established
to reflect the financial transactions in respect of the program, as maintained by the FMPU.
Scope
The audit will be carried out in accordance with International Standards of Auditing, and will include
such tests and controls as the auditor considers necessary under the circumstances. In addition, the auditor
should pay special attention to the following:
(a)    All external funds have been used in accordance with the conditions of the relevant financing
agreements, with due attention to economy and efficiency, and only for the purposes for which
the financing was provided. Relevant financing agreement are the IDA Credit No ............. of
US$ .     for 3 years, the ADF Loan No. of U.A . ..... for 3 years, and likely other donors';
(b)    Counterpart funds have been provided and used in accordance with the relevant financing
agreements, due attention to economy and efficiency, and only for the purpose for which they
were provided;
(c)    Goods and services financed have been procured in accordance with the relevant financing
agreement;
(d)    All necessary supporting documents, records, and accounts have been kept in respect of all
program ventures [including expenditures reported via SOEs or SAs]. Clear linkages should exits
between the books of account and reports presented to the contributing donors.
(e)    The Credit account reconciliation between the amount shown as "received by the Program from
such donor" and shown as being disbursed by the Bank has been properly prepared and is
presented as an annex to the PFS. This reconciliation statement should indicate the mechanism of
disbursement, i.e, Special Account, Statement of Expenditures, or direct payments.



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                       Attachment 8: Page 2 of 4
(f)    The program accounts have been prepared in accordance with consistently applied International
Accounting Standards and give a true and fair view of the financial situation of the program as of
June 30, December 31, 1999, 2000, 2001 and of resources and expenditures for the semi-annual
years ended on those dates.
Program Financial Statements
The Program Financial Statements should include:
(a)    a Statement of Source (summary of funds received, showing the World Bank, ADB other donors
funds, Government Counterpart funds, and beneficiary contribution separately) and Application
of Funds (summary of Expenditures shown under the main program headings and by main
categories of expenditures for the current year);
(b)    a Balance Sheet showing Accumulated Funds of the Program, bank balances, fixed assets,
inventories, other assets of the program, and liabilities, if any; and
(c)    notes to the financial statements presenting background information on the program, the
accounting principles, details analysis and relevant explanation of the main accounts/major
balances, etc.
Statements of Expenditures
In addition to the audit of the PFS, the auditor is required to audit all SOEs used during the year under
review as the basis for the submission of withdrawal applications. The auditor should apply such tests and
controls as the auditor considers necessary under the circumstances, ensuring that the existing internal
control procedures for the preparation and processing of the said SOEs are sound and reliable. The
auditor should examine carefully the expenditures to ensure that: i) they are genuine program
expenditures and eligible with regard to the relevant financing agreement and with reference to the
program documents of the donors for guidance when considered necessary; and ii) they are reasonable
with respect to the planned activities included in the annual work program and budget. Where ineligible
expenditures are identified as having been included in withdrawal applications and reimbursed against,
there should be a schedule listing individual SOE withdrawal applications for specific reference number
and amount. The total withdrawals under the SOE procedure should agree with the overall reconciliation
of bank disbursements prepared by the program and described above. A separate opinion to that effect
will be issued by the auditor as indicated in the introductory paragraph.
Special Accounts
In conjunction with the audit of the Program Financial Statement, the auditor is also required to prepare a
Special Account reconciliation and audit the activities on the Special Accounts associated with the
Program. The Special Account usually comprise but is not limited to:



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                      Attachment 8: Page 3 of 4
* deposit and replenishments received from the donors
* payment substantiated by withdrawal applications
* interest that may be earned from the balances and which belong to the borrower; and
* the remaining balances at the end of the fiscal year.
The auditor must form a separate opinion as to the degree of compliance with the Bank's procedures and
the balance of the Special Account at the year-end. The audit should examine the eligibility and
correctness and financial transactions during the period under review and fund balances at the end of such
a period, the operation and use of the SA in accordance with the financing agreement, and the adequacy
of internal controls for this type of disbursement mechanism.
For the program, the Special Accounts are referred to in legal agreements between the donors and the
Government of Sierra Leone. Special Accounts statements and the auditor's separate opinion thereon
should accompany the Program Financial Statements.
Internal Control System
The auditor is required to perform an in-depth and comprehensive review of the program internal control
system. Such a review would be larger in scope than what is normally required for ordinary audits. The
objective of the review is to provide the auditor with sufficient understanding of the rules and procedures
of the internal control system, including the existing administrative, accounting, financial, and budgetary
Manual of procedures, and to determine whether the said rules and procedures are adequate, reliable, and
operating correctly. In this vein, the auditor should assess with particular attention and determine
whether: i) the computerized financial accounting, and reporting system in place is appropriate; ii) the
accounting and financial staff within the FMPU is capable of managing the program efficiently using the
computerized system. The findings and observations of the auditor should be presented in a separate
report, the Management Letter, addressed along with the audit report to the borrower's representative.
The Management Letter should highlight all the weaknesses in the program internal control system,
assess the inherent risks associated with the internal control shortcomings, and make practical and
relevant recommendations to improve the system as well as to enhance the managerial skills and
capability of the accounting and financial staff. In the Management Letter, the auditor will, inter-alia:
(a)    give comments and observations on the accounting records, systems and controls that were
examined during the course of the audit;
(b)   identify specific deficiencies and areas of weakness in systems and controls and make
recommendation for their improvement;
(c)   report on the degree of compliance of each of the financial covenants on the financing agreement
and give comments, if any, on internal and external matters affecting such compliance;
(d)    communicate matter that have come to attention during the audit which might have a significant
impact on the implementation of the project;
(e)    bring to the borrower's attention any other matters that auditors considers pertinent.



Technical Annex                                     Community Reintegration and Rehabilitation
Sierra Leone                                                       Attachment 8: Page 4 of 4
Interim Audit
The auditor is required to carry out an interim audit (after 9 months of activities) for each year.
He should perform during the interim audit: i) a comprehensive review of the internal control system,
ii) an assessment of the proper recording/accounting of the transactions, and iii) an in-depth review of the
Statement of Expenditures up to that date (the review of the remaining months should be carried out
during annual audits). The auditor should prepare an interim audit report as a result of his audit to be
discussed with the Program Coordinator before distribution by the latter to the donors.
Audit Report
The auditor is required to prepare and produce for each annual audit:
a)    the audit report/short forrn report containing: i) the auditor professional opinion on the Project
Financial Statements, the actual audited financial statements, and the notes to the audited
Financial Statements; ii) a separate opinion on the SOEs along with a schedule of SOEs used
during the fiscal year (sequence number, date, description, and amount) and commenting on the
accuracy and propriety of expenditures withdrawn under SOEs procedures and the extend to
which the Bank can rely on SOEs as a basis for credit disbursement; and iii) a separate opinion
on the Special Accounts commenting on the degree of compliance with the Bank's procedures
and the eligibility and correctness of the financial transactions through the Special Account
during the year, and
b)    the Management Letter reporting on the major internal control weakness as well as managerial
deficiencies and making relevant and practical recommendations for improvement.
The auditor should submit the audit report (short form) and the Management Letter to the borrower's
designated representative within six (6) months of the end of the fiscal year. The latter should transmit
copies to the Ministry of Finance and promptly forward three (3) copies to each donor.
General
The auditor should be given access to and he should consult all legal documents (Loan/Grant
Agreements), Appraisal Reports, supervision reports, correspondences, and any other information
associated with the project and deemed necessary by the auditor.
It is highly desirable that the auditor become familiar with the donors' guidelines on financial reporting
and auditing of projects which summarize their financial reporting and auditing requirements. The auditor
should also be familiar with the donors' disbursement manuals. Those documents will be provided by the
Financial Manager of the FMPU.
